<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Fossil fuel</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Fuel formed over millions of years from dead plants and animals</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Oil and gas" redirects here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Oil_and_gas_(disambiguation)" title="Oil and gas (disambiguation)">Oil and gas (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:217px;max-width:217px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:215px;max-width:215px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:159px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chuhuo.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Chuhuo.jpg/213px-Chuhuo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Chuhuo.jpg/320px-Chuhuo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Chuhuo.jpg/426px-Chuhuo.jpg 2x" width="213"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:215px;max-width:215px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:212px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Petroleum_sample.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2443" data-file-width="2444" decoding="async" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Petroleum_sample.jpg/213px-Petroleum_sample.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Petroleum_sample.jpg/320px-Petroleum_sample.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Petroleum_sample.jpg/426px-Petroleum_sample.jpg 2x" width="213"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:215px;max-width:215px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:142px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bituminous_Coal.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="4608" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Bituminous_Coal.JPG/213px-Bituminous_Coal.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Bituminous_Coal.JPG/320px-Bituminous_Coal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Bituminous_Coal.JPG/426px-Bituminous_Coal.JPG 2x" width="213"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">The main fossil fuels: gas, oil and coal.</div></div></div></div>
<p>A <b>fossil fuel</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">hydrocarbon</a>-containing material formed naturally in the <a href="/wiki/Earth%27s_crust" title="Earth's crust">earth's crust</a> from the remains of dead plants and animals that is extracted and <a href="/wiki/Combustion" title="Combustion">burned</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Fuel" title="Fuel">fuel</a>. The main fossil fuels are <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crude_oil" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Fossil fuels may be burned to provide heat for use directly (such as for cooking or heating), to power engines (such as <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engines</a> in motor vehicles), or to <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">generate electricity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Some fossil fuels are refined into derivatives such as <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">kerosene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a> and <a href="/wiki/Propane" title="Propane">propane</a> before burning. The origin of fossil fuels is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anaerobic_decomposition" title="Anaerobic decomposition">anaerobic decomposition</a> of buried dead <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organisms</a>, containing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organic_molecules" title="Organic molecules">organic molecules</a> created by <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">photosynthesis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thermochemistry_of_formation_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-thermochemistry_of_formation-3">[3]</a></sup> The conversion from these materials to high-carbon fossil fuels typically require a geological process of millions of years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019, 84% of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_energy_consumption" title="World energy consumption">primary energy consumption in the world</a> and 64% of its electricity was from fossil fuels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The large-scale burning of fossil fuels causes serious <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_the_energy_industry#Fossil_fuel_use" title="Environmental impact of the energy industry">environmental damage</a>. Over 80% of the <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> (CO<sub>2</sub>) generated by human activity comes from burning them: around 35 billion <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">tonnes</a> a year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> compared to 4 billion from <a href="/wiki/Land_development" title="Land development">land development</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carbon_cycle" title="Carbon cycle">Natural processes</a> on Earth, mostly <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_carbon_cycle" title="Oceanic carbon cycle">absorption by the ocean</a>, can only remove a small part of this. Therefore, there is a net increase of many billion tonnes of atmospheric carbon dioxide per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Although <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methane_leaks" title="Methane leaks">methane leaks</a> are significant,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 52">: 52 </span></sup> the burning of fossil fuels is the main source of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions causing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">ocean acidification</a>. Additionally, most air pollution deaths are due to fossil fuel <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">particulates</a> and noxious gases. It is estimated that this costs over 3% of global GDP<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-10">[10]</a></sup> and that <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_phase-out" title="Fossil fuel phase-out">fossil fuel phase-out</a> would save millions of lives each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>Recognition of the <a href="/wiki/Climate_crisis" title="Climate crisis">climate crisis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">pollution</a> and other negative impacts caused by fossil fuels has led to a widespread <a href="/wiki/Energy_transition" title="Energy transition">policy transition</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_movement" title="Climate movement">activist movement</a> focused on <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_phase-out" title="Fossil fuel phase-out">ending their use</a> in favor of <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">sustainable energy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> However, because the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_industry" title="Fossil fuel industry">fossil fuel industry</a> is so heavily integrated in the global economy and <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_subsidies" title="Fossil fuel subsidies">heavily subsidized</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> this transition is expected to have significant economic impacts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Many stakeholders argue that this change needs to be a <a href="/wiki/Just_transition" title="Just transition">just transition</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and create policy that addresses the societal burdens created by the <a href="/wiki/Stranded_asset" title="Stranded asset">stranded assets</a> of the fossil fuel industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>International policy, in the form of United Nations <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_7" title="Sustainable Development Goal 7">Sustainable Development Goal 7: Affordable and Clean Energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_13" title="Sustainable Development Goal 13">Sustainable Development Goal 13: Climate Action</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Climate Agreement</a>, is designed to facilitate this transition at a global level. In 2021, the <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a> concluded that no new <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_exploration" title="Hydrocarbon exploration">fossil fuel extraction projects could be opened</a> if the global economy and society wants to avoid the worst <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change" title="Effects of climate change">impacts of climate change</a> and meet international goals for <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">climate change mitigation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin">Origin</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Countries_by_Oil_Production_in_2013.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="863" decoding="async" height="92" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Countries_by_Oil_Production_in_2013.svg/200px-Countries_by_Oil_Production_in_2013.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Countries_by_Oil_Production_in_2013.svg/300px-Countries_by_Oil_Production_in_2013.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Countries_by_Oil_Production_in_2013.svg/400px-Countries_by_Oil_Production_in_2013.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Countries_by_Oil_Production_in_2013.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crude_oil" title="Crude oil">oil fields</a> are located only at certain places on earth,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> only some countries are oil-independent; the other countries depend on the oil-production capacities of these countries</div></div></div>
<p>The theory that fossil fuels formed from the <a href="/wiki/Fossil" title="Fossil">fossilized remains</a> of dead plants by exposure to heat and pressure in <a href="/wiki/Earth%27s_crust" title="Earth's crust">Earth's crust</a> over millions of years was first introduced by <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Libavius" title="Andreas Libavius">Andreas Libavius</a> "in his 1597 Alchemia [Alchymia]" and later by <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lomonosov" title="Mikhail Lomonosov">Mikhail Lomonosov</a> "as early as 1757 and certainly by 1763".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>  The first use of the term "fossil fuel" occurs in the work of the German chemist <a href="/wiki/Caspar_Neumann" title="Caspar Neumann">Caspar Neumann</a>, in English translation in 1759.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NeumannLewis1773_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-NeumannLewis1773-21">[21]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i> notes that in the phrase "fossil fuel" the adjective "fossil" means "[o]btained by digging; found buried in the earth", which dates to at least 1652,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> before the English noun "fossil" came to refer primarily to long-dead organisms in the early 18th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>Aquatic <a href="/wiki/Phytoplankton" title="Phytoplankton">phytoplankton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zooplankton" title="Zooplankton">zooplankton</a> that died and sedimented in large quantities under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anoxic_sea_water" title="Anoxic sea water">anoxic conditions</a> millions of years ago began forming petroleum and natural gas as a result of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anaerobic_decomposition" title="Anaerobic decomposition">anaerobic decomposition</a>. Over <a href="/wiki/Geologic_time_scale" title="Geologic time scale">geological time</a> this <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">organic</a> <a href="/wiki/Matter" title="Matter">matter</a>, mixed with <a href="/wiki/Mud" title="Mud">mud</a>, became buried under further heavy layers of inorganic sediment. The resulting high temperature and <a href="/wiki/Pressure" title="Pressure">pressure</a> caused the organic matter to chemically <a href="/wiki/Diagenesis" title="Diagenesis">alter</a>, first into a waxy material known as <a href="/wiki/Kerogen" title="Kerogen">kerogen</a>, which is found in <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale" title="Oil shale">oil shales</a>, and then with more heat into liquid and gaseous hydrocarbons in a process known as <a href="/wiki/Catagenesis_(geology)" title="Catagenesis (geology)">catagenesis</a>. Despite these heat-driven transformations, the energy released in combustion is still photosynthetic in origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thermochemistry_of_formation_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-thermochemistry_of_formation-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Terrestrial_plant" title="Terrestrial plant">Terrestrial plants</a> tended to form coal and methane. Many of the coal fields date to the <a href="/wiki/Carboniferous" title="Carboniferous">Carboniferous</a> period of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Earth" title="History of Earth">Earth's history</a>. Terrestrial plants also form <a href="/wiki/Kerogen#Type_III" title="Kerogen">type III kerogen</a>, a source of natural gas. Although fossil fuels are continually formed by natural processes, they are classified as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-renewable_resources" title="Non-renewable resources">non-renewable resources</a> because they take millions of years to form and known viable reserves are being depleted much faster than new ones are generated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Importance">Importance</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grangemouth04nov06.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="750" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Grangemouth04nov06.jpg/170px-Grangemouth04nov06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Grangemouth04nov06.jpg/255px-Grangemouth04nov06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Grangemouth04nov06.jpg/340px-Grangemouth04nov06.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grangemouth04nov06.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A petrochemical refinery in <a href="/wiki/Grangemouth" title="Grangemouth">Grangemouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, UK</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_power_station" title="Fossil fuel power station">Fossil fuel power station</a></div>
<p>Fossil fuels have been important to human development because they can be readily burned in the open atmosphere to produce heat. The use of <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> as a domestic fuel predates recorded history. Coal was burned in some early furnaces for the <a href="/wiki/Smelting" title="Smelting">smelting</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metal_ore" title="Metal ore">metal ore</a>, while semi-solid hydrocarbons from oil seeps were also burned in ancient times,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> they were mostly used for waterproofing and <a href="/wiki/Embalming" title="Embalming">embalming</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>Commercial exploitation of petroleum began in the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>Natural gas, once <a href="/wiki/Gas_flare" title="Gas flare">flared-off</a> as an unneeded byproduct of petroleum production, is now considered a very valuable resource.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Natural gas deposits are also the main source of <a href="/wiki/Helium" title="Helium">helium</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Heavy_crude_oil" title="Heavy crude oil">Heavy crude oil</a>, which is much more viscous than conventional crude oil, and <a href="/wiki/Oil_sands" title="Oil sands">oil sands</a>, where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bitumen" title="Bitumen">bitumen</a> is found mixed with sand and clay, began to become more important as sources of fossil fuel in the early  2000s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale" title="Oil shale">Oil shale</a> and similar materials are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sedimentary" title="Sedimentary">sedimentary</a> rocks containing <a href="/wiki/Kerogen" title="Kerogen">kerogen</a>, a complex mixture of high-molecular weight organic compounds, which yield <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_fuel" title="Synthetic fuel">synthetic crude oil</a> when heated (<a href="/wiki/Pyrolysis" title="Pyrolysis">pyrolyzed</a>). With additional processing, they can be employed instead of other established fossil fuels. During the 2010s and 2020s there was <a href="/wiki/Disinvestment" title="Disinvestment">disinvestment</a> from exploitation of such resources due to their high <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">carbon cost</a> relative to more easily-processed reserves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>Prior to the latter half of the 18th century, <a href="/wiki/Windmill" title="Windmill">windmills</a> and <a href="/wiki/Watermill" title="Watermill">watermills</a> provided the energy needed for work such as milling flour, <a href="/wiki/Sawmill" title="Sawmill">sawing wood</a> or pumping water, while burning wood or <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> provided domestic heat. The wide-scale use of fossil fuels, coal at first and petroleum later, in <a href="/wiki/Steam_engine" title="Steam engine">steam engines</a> enabled the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>. At the same time, <a href="/wiki/Gas_lighting" title="Gas lighting">gas lights</a> using natural gas or <a href="/wiki/Coal_gas" title="Coal gas">coal gas</a> were coming into wide use. The invention of the <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> and its use in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">automobiles</a> and trucks greatly increased the demand for gasoline and <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">diesel oil</a>, both made from fossil fuels. Other forms of transportation, railways and aircraft, also require fossil fuels. The other major use for fossil fuels is in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_power_industry" title="Electrical power industry">generating electricity</a> and as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feedstock" title="Feedstock">feedstock</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical_industry" title="Petrochemical industry">petrochemical industry</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tar" title="Tar">Tar</a>, a leftover of petroleum extraction, is used in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Road_construction" title="Road construction">construction of roads</a>.
</p><p>The energy for the <a href="/wiki/Green_Revolution" title="Green Revolution">Green Revolution</a> was provided by fossil fuels in the form of <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizers</a> (natural gas), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pesticides" title="Pesticides">pesticides</a> (oil), and <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">hydrocarbon</a> fueled <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The development of synthetic nitrogen fertilizer has significantly supported global <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a> — it has been estimated that almost half the people on the Earth are currently fed as a result of synthetic nitrogen fertilizer use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> According to ICIS Fertilizers managing editor Julia Meehan, "People don’t realise that 50% of the world’s food relies on fertilisers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg/170px-Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg/255px-Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg/340px-Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An oil well in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_effects">Environmental effects</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CO2_Emissions_by_Source_Since_1880.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="635" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/CO2_Emissions_by_Source_Since_1880.svg/300px-CO2_Emissions_by_Source_Since_1880.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/CO2_Emissions_by_Source_Since_1880.svg/450px-CO2_Emissions_by_Source_Since_1880.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/CO2_Emissions_by_Source_Since_1880.svg/600px-CO2_Emissions_by_Source_Since_1880.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CO2_Emissions_by_Source_Since_1880.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Global_Carbon_Project" title="Global Carbon Project">Global Carbon Project</a> shows how additions to CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub> since 1880 have been caused by different sources ramping up one after another.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change" title="Effects of climate change">Effects of climate change</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_and_environmental_impact_of_the_coal_industry" title="Health and environmental impact of the coal industry">Health and environmental impact of the coal industry</a></div>
<p>The burning of fossil fuels has a number of negative <a href="/wiki/Externality" title="Externality">externalities</a> – harmful environmental impacts where the effects extend beyond the people using the fuel. The actual effects depend on the fuel in question. All fossil fuels release CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub> when they burn, thus accelerating <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.  Burning coal, and to a lesser extent oil and its derivatives, contribute to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atmospheric_particulate_matter" title="Atmospheric particulate matter">atmospheric particulate matter</a>, smog and <a href="/wiki/Acid_rain" title="Acid rain">acid rain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CQ_Researcher_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-CQ_Researcher-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mitigations_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mitigations-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Common_Era_Temperature.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Common_Era_Temperature.svg/300px-Common_Era_Temperature.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Common_Era_Temperature.svg/450px-Common_Era_Temperature.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Common_Era_Temperature.svg/600px-Common_Era_Temperature.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Common_Era_Temperature.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Global surface temperature reconstruction over the last 2000 years using proxy data from tree rings, corals, and ice cores in blue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Directly observational data is in red, with all data showing a 5 year moving average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa_temperatures_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa_temperatures-40">[40]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="635" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg/300px-20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg/450px-20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg/600px-20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 2020, renewables overtook fossil fuels as the European Union's main source of electricity for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EmberEUpower_20210125_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-EmberEUpower_20210125-41">[41]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Climate change is largely driven by the release of greenhouse gasses like CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub>, with the burning of fossil fuels being the main source of these emissions. In most parts of the world climate change is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_ecosystems" title="Climate change and ecosystems">negatively impacting ecosystems</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> This includes contributing to the extinction of species (see also <a href="/wiki/Extinction_risk_from_climate_change" title="Extinction risk from climate change">extinction risk from climate change</a>) and reducing people's ability to produce food, thus adding to the problem of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_hunger" title="World hunger">world hunger</a>. Continued rises in global temperatures will lead to further adverse <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming" title="Effects of global warming">effects</a> on both ecosystems and people, with the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> having stated climate change is the greatest threat to human health in the 21st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>
</p><p>Combustion of fossil fuels generates <a href="/wiki/Sulfuric_acid" title="Sulfuric acid">sulfuric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nitric_acid" title="Nitric acid">nitric acids</a>, which fall to Earth as acid rain, impacting both natural areas and the built environment. Monuments and sculptures made from <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> are particularly vulnerable, as the acids dissolve <a href="/wiki/Calcium_carbonate" title="Calcium carbonate">calcium carbonate</a>.
</p><p>Fossil fuels also contain radioactive materials, mainly <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thorium" title="Thorium">thorium</a>, which are released into the atmosphere. In 2000, about 12,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tonnes" title="Tonnes">tonnes</a> of thorium and 5,000 tonnes of uranium were released worldwide from burning coal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> It is estimated that during 1982, US coal burning released 155 times as much radioactivity into the atmosphere as the <a href="/wiki/Three_Mile_Island_accident" title="Three Mile Island accident">Three Mile Island accident</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p><p>Burning coal also generates large amounts of <a href="/wiki/Bottom_ash" title="Bottom ash">bottom ash</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fly_ash" title="Fly ash">fly ash</a>. These materials are used in a wide variety of applications (see <a href="/wiki/Fly_ash#Reuse" title="Fly ash">Fly ash reuse</a>), utilizing, for example, about 40% of the United States production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to the effects that result from burning, the harvesting, processing, and distribution of fossil fuels also have environmental effects. Coal mining methods, particularly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountaintop_removal" title="Mountaintop removal">mountaintop removal</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strip_mining" title="Strip mining">strip mining</a>, have negative environmental impacts, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Offshore_oil_drilling" title="Offshore oil drilling">offshore oil drilling</a> poses a hazard to aquatic organisms. Fossil fuel wells can contribute to methane release via <a href="/wiki/Fugitive_gas_emissions" title="Fugitive gas emissions">fugitive gas emissions</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_refineries" title="Oil refineries">Oil refineries</a> also have negative environmental impacts, including air and water pollution. Coal is sometimes transported by diesel-powered locomotives, while crude oil is typically transported by tanker ships, requiring the combustion of additional fossil fuels.
</p><p>A variety of mitigating efforts have arisen to counter the negative effects of fossil fuels. This includes a movement to use alternative energy sources, such as <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_regulation" title="Environmental regulation">Environmental regulation</a> uses a variety of approaches to limit these emissions; for example, rules against releasing waste products like fly ash into the atmosphere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mitigations_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mitigations-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2020, the United Nations released a report saying that despite the need to reduce greenhouse emissions, various governments are "<a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/double_down" title="wikt:double down">doubling down</a>" on fossil fuels, in some cases diverting over 50% of their COVID-19 recovery <a href="/wiki/Stimulus_(economics)" title="Stimulus (economics)">stimulus</a> funding to fossil fuel production rather than to alternative energy. The UN secretary general <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a> declared that "Humanity is waging war on nature. This is suicidal. Nature always strikes back – and it is already doing so with growing force and fury." However, Guterres also said there is still cause for hope, anticipating <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a>'s plan for the US to join other large emitters like China and the EU in adopting targets to reach <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Net_zero" title="Net zero">net zero</a> emissions by 2050.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Illness_and_deaths">Illness and deaths</span></h2>
<p>Environmental pollution from fossil fuels impacts humans because <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">particulates</a> and other air pollution from fossil fuel combustion cause illness and death when inhaled. These health effects include premature death, acute respiratory illness, aggravated asthma, chronic bronchitis and decreased lung function. The poor, undernourished, very young and very old, and people with preexisting respiratory disease and other ill health are more at risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Global air pollution deaths due to fossil fuels in 2018 have been estimated at over 8 million people, nearly 1 in 5 deaths worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>While all energy sources inherently have adverse effects, the data shows that fossil fuels cause the highest levels of greenhouse gas emissions and are the most dangerous for human health. In contrast, modern renewable energy sources appear to be safer for human health and cleaner. The death rate from accidents and air pollution in the EU are as follows per terawatt-hour: coal (24.6 deaths), oil (18.4 deaths), natural gas (2.8 deaths), biomass (4.6 deaths), hydropower (0.02 deaths), nuclear energy (0.07 deaths), wind (0.04 deaths), and solar (0.02 deaths). The greenhouse gas emissions from each energy source are as follows, measured in tonnes: coal (820 tonnes), oil (720 tonnes), natural gas (490 tonnes), biomass (78–230 tonnes), hydropower (34 tonnes), nuclear energy (3 tonnes), wind (4 tonnes), and solar (5 tonnes).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> As the data shows, coal, oil, natural gas, and biomass cause higher death rates and higher levels of greenhouse gas emissions than hydropower, nuclear energy, wind, and solar power. Scientists propose that 1.8 million lives have been saved by replacing fossil fuel sources with nuclear power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phase-out">Phase-out</span></h2>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This paragraph is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_phase-out" title="Fossil fuel phase-out">Fossil fuel phase-out</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p><a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_phase-out" title="Fossil fuel phase-out">Fossil fuel phase-out</a> is the gradual reduction of the use and production of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" title="Fossil fuels">fossil fuels</a> to zero.
</p>
It is part of the ongoing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_transition" title="Renewable energy transition">renewable energy transition</a>. Current efforts in fossil fuel phase-out involve replacing fossil fuels with <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">sustainable energy</a> sources in sectors such as <a href="/wiki/Transport" title="Transport">transport</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heating" title="Heating">heating</a>. Alternatives to fossil fuels include <a href="/wiki/Electrification" title="Electrification">electrification</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_hydrogen" title="Green hydrogen">green hydrogen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a>. Phase-out policies include both demand-side and supply-side constraints.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Whereas demand-side approaches seek to reduce fossil-fuel consumption, supply-side initiatives seek to constraint production to accelerate the pace of energy transition and reduction in emissions.</div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Just_transition">Just transition</span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Just_transition" title="Just transition">Just transition</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Just_transition&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Just_Transition._Decarbonisation_-Melbourneclimatestrike_IMG_5369_(48764789363).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1347" data-file-width="858" decoding="async" height="345" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Just_Transition._Decarbonisation_-Melbourneclimatestrike_IMG_5369_%2848764789363%29.jpg/220px-Just_Transition._Decarbonisation_-Melbourneclimatestrike_IMG_5369_%2848764789363%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Just_Transition._Decarbonisation_-Melbourneclimatestrike_IMG_5369_%2848764789363%29.jpg/330px-Just_Transition._Decarbonisation_-Melbourneclimatestrike_IMG_5369_%2848764789363%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Just_Transition._Decarbonisation_-Melbourneclimatestrike_IMG_5369_%2848764789363%29.jpg/440px-Just_Transition._Decarbonisation_-Melbourneclimatestrike_IMG_5369_%2848764789363%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Just_Transition._Decarbonisation_-Melbourneclimatestrike_IMG_5369_(48764789363).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protestor in Melbourne calling for a just transition and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decarbonisation" title="Decarbonisation">decarbonisation</a></div></div></div>
<a href="/wiki/Just_transition" title="Just transition">Just transition</a> is a framework developed by the <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade union</a> movement<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Just_transition_:0_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Just_transition_:0-56">[56]</a></sup> to encompass a range of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_intervention" title="Social intervention">social interventions</a> needed to secure <a href="/wiki/Labor_rights" title="Labor rights">workers' rights</a> and livelihoods when economies are shifting to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sustainable_production" title="Sustainable production">sustainable production</a>, primarily <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">combating climate change</a> and protecting <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>. In Europe, advocates for a just transition want to unite social and <a href="/wiki/Climate_justice" title="Climate justice">climate justice</a>, for example, for coal workers in coal-dependent developing regions who lack employment opportunities beyond coal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Divestment">Divestment</span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_divestment" title="Fossil fuel divestment">Fossil fuel divestment</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_divestment&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Divestment_growth_en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Divestment_growth_en.svg/300px-Divestment_growth_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Divestment_growth_en.svg/450px-Divestment_growth_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Divestment_growth_en.svg/600px-Divestment_growth_en.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Divestment_growth_en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>As of 2021, 1,300 institutions possessing 14.6 trillion dollars divested from the fossil fuel industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuel_divestment_Commitments_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuel_divestment_Commitments-58">[58]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_divestment" title="Fossil fuel divestment">Fossil fuel divestment</a> or fossil fuel divestment and investment in climate solutions is an attempt to reduce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">climate change</a> by exerting social, political, and economic pressure for the institutional <a href="/wiki/Divestment" title="Divestment">divestment</a> of assets including stocks, bonds, and other financial instruments connected to companies involved in extracting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" title="Fossil fuels">fossil fuels</a>.
</p><p>Fossil fuel divestment campaigns emerged on campuses in the United States in 2011 with students urging their administrations to turn <a href="/wiki/Financial_endowment" title="Financial endowment">endowment</a> investments in the <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel#industry" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel industry</a> into investments in clean energy and communities <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_vulnerability" title="Climate change vulnerability">most impacted by climate change</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuel_divestment_Shifting_Discourse_on_Climate_and_Sustainability:_Key_Characteristics_of_the_Higher_Education_Fossil_Fuel_Divestment_Movement_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuel_divestment_Shifting_Discourse_on_Climate_and_Sustainability:_Key_Characteristics_of_the_Higher_Education_Fossil_Fuel_Divestment_Movement-59">[59]</a></sup> In 2012, Unity College in Maine became the first institution of higher learning to divest<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> its endowment from fossil fuels.
</p>
By 2015, fossil fuel divestment was reportedly the fastest growing <a href="/wiki/Financial_endowment#Divestment_campaigns" title="Financial endowment">divestment movement</a> in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuel_divestment_Guardian2015_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuel_divestment_Guardian2015-61">[61]</a></sup> In October 2021, a total of 1,485 institutions representing $39.2 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trillion_(short_scale)" title="Trillion (short scale)">trillion</a> in assets worldwide had begun or committed to a divestment from fossil fuels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></div></div><div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20210119_Renewable_energy_investment_-_2004-_BloombergNEF.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="575" data-file-width="850" decoding="async" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/20210119_Renewable_energy_investment_-_2004-_BloombergNEF.svg/330px-20210119_Renewable_energy_investment_-_2004-_BloombergNEF.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/20210119_Renewable_energy_investment_-_2004-_BloombergNEF.svg/495px-20210119_Renewable_energy_investment_-_2004-_BloombergNEF.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/20210119_Renewable_energy_investment_-_2004-_BloombergNEF.svg/660px-20210119_Renewable_energy_investment_-_2004-_BloombergNEF.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20210119_Renewable_energy_investment_-_2004-_BloombergNEF.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Investment: Companies, governments and households invested $501.3 billion in decarbonization in 2020, including renewable energy (solar, wind), electric vehicles and associated charging infrastructure, energy storage, energy-efficient heating systems, carbon capture and storage, and hydrogen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuel_phase-out_BloombergNEF_20210119_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuel_phase-out_BloombergNEF_20210119-63">[63]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_(LCOE,_Lazard)_-_renewable_energy.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1150" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_%28LCOE%2C_Lazard%29_-_renewable_energy.svg/330px-20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_%28LCOE%2C_Lazard%29_-_renewable_energy.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_%28LCOE%2C_Lazard%29_-_renewable_energy.svg/495px-20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_%28LCOE%2C_Lazard%29_-_renewable_energy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_%28LCOE%2C_Lazard%29_-_renewable_energy.svg/660px-20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_%28LCOE%2C_Lazard%29_-_renewable_energy.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_(LCOE,_Lazard)_-_renewable_energy.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cost: With increasingly widespread implementation of renewable energy sources, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Levelized_cost_of_energy" title="Levelized cost of energy">costs</a> have declined, most notably for energy generated by solar panels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuel_phase-out_PopSciLazard_LCOE2020_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuel_phase-out_PopSciLazard_LCOE2020-64">[64]</a></sup><br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Levelized_cost_of_energy" title="Levelized cost of energy">Levelized cost of energy</a> (LCOE) is a measure of the average net present cost of electricity generation for a generating plant over its lifetime.</div></div></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_sector">Industrial sector</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coal_industry" title="Coal industry">Coal industry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry" title="Petroleum industry">Petroleum industry</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_exporters" title="Fossil fuel exporters">Fossil fuel exporters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels_lobby" title="Fossil fuels lobby">Fossil fuels lobby</a></div><p>In 2019, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Aramco" title="Saudi Aramco">Saudi Aramco</a> was listed and it reached a US$2 trillion valuation on its second day of trading,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kerr2019_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr2019-65">[65]</a></sup> after the world's largest initial public offering.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raval2019_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Raval2019-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_effects">Economic effects</span></h3>
<p>Air pollution from fossil fuels in 2018 has been estimated to cost US$2.9 trillion, or 3.3% of global GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsidies">Subsidies</span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_subsidies" title="Fossil fuel subsidies">Fossil fuel subsidies</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_subsidies&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fossil-fuel-subsidies-per-capita.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="850" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Fossil-fuel-subsidies-per-capita.svg/220px-Fossil-fuel-subsidies-per-capita.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Fossil-fuel-subsidies-per-capita.svg/330px-Fossil-fuel-subsidies-per-capita.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Fossil-fuel-subsidies-per-capita.svg/440px-Fossil-fuel-subsidies-per-capita.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fossil-fuel-subsidies-per-capita.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fossil-fuel subsidies per capita, 2019. Fossil-fuel pre-tax subsidies per capita are measured in constant US dollars.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fossil-fuel-subsidies-gdp.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="850" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Fossil-fuel-subsidies-gdp.svg/220px-Fossil-fuel-subsidies-gdp.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Fossil-fuel-subsidies-gdp.svg/330px-Fossil-fuel-subsidies-gdp.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Fossil-fuel-subsidies-gdp.svg/440px-Fossil-fuel-subsidies-gdp.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fossil-fuel-subsidies-gdp.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fossil-fuel subsidies as a share of GDP, 2019. Fossil-fuel pre-tax subsidies are given as a share of total gross domestic product.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_subsidies" title="Fossil fuel subsidies">Fossil fuel subsidies</a> are <a href="/wiki/Energy_subsidy" title="Energy subsidy">energy subsidies</a> on fossil fuels. They may be <a href="/wiki/Tax_break" title="Tax break">tax breaks</a> on <a href="/wiki/Consumption_(economics)" title="Consumption (economics)">consumption</a>, such as a lower <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">sales tax</a> on <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> for <a href="/wiki/Heating,_ventilation,_and_air_conditioning" title="Heating, ventilation, and air conditioning">residential heating</a>; or <a href="/wiki/Subsidy" title="Subsidy">subsidies</a> on <a href="/wiki/Production_(economics)" title="Production (economics)">production</a>, such as  tax breaks on <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_exploration" title="Hydrocarbon exploration">exploration for oil</a>. Or they may be free or cheap <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Negative_Externalities" title="Negative Externalities">negative externalities</a>; such as <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a> or <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> due to burning <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">diesel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jet_fuel" title="Jet fuel">jet fuel</a>. Some fossil fuel subsidies are via <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">electricity generation</a>, such as subsidies for <a href="/wiki/Coal-fired_power_station" title="Coal-fired power station">coal-fired power stations</a>. One downside to subsidizing any industry is that competition and innovation are lessened or lost completely. Subsidizing can make a product be cheaper for buyers, but in the long run, innovation and lower prices come from a competitive free market. 
</p><p>Despite the <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20 countries</a> having pledged to phase-out inefficient fossil fuel subsidies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup>  they may be continued because of voter demand<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> or for <a href="/wiki/Energy_security" title="Energy security">energy security</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuel_subsidies_:1_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuel_subsidies_:1-69">[69]</a></sup> Global fossil fuel consumption subsidies in 2021 have been estimated at 440 billion dollars;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuel_subsidies_:4_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuel_subsidies_:4-70">[70]</a></sup> although they vary each year depending on <a href="/wiki/Price_of_oil" title="Price of oil">oil prices</a> they are consistently hundreds of billions of dollars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuel_subsidies_:5_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuel_subsidies_:5-71">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
Eliminating fossil fuel subsidies would greatly reduce global <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_emissions" title="Carbon emissions">carbon emissions</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuel_subsidies_Coady2017_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuel_subsidies_Coady2017-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuel_subsidies_NYT12515_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuel_subsidies_NYT12515-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuel_subsidies_:02_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuel_subsidies_:02-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> and would reduce the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_risks_of_air_pollution" title="Health risks of air pollution">health risks of air pollution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> As of 2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, policy researchers estimate that substantially more money is spent on fossil fuel subsidies than on environmentally harmful <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_subsidy" title="Agricultural subsidy">agricultural subsidies</a> or environmentally harmful <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Water_subsidies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Water subsidies (page does not exist)">water subsidies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lobbying_activities">Lobbying activities</span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">These paragraphs are an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels_lobby" title="Fossil fuels lobby">Fossil fuels lobby</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuels_lobby&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels_lobby" title="Fossil fuels lobby">Fossil fuels lobby</a>" is a term used to label the <a href="/wiki/Lobbying" title="Lobbying">paid representatives</a> of corporations involved in the fossil fuel industry (<a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry" title="Petroleum industry">oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">gas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>), as well as related industries like <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemicals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plastics_industry" title="Plastics industry">plastics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aviation" title="Aviation">aviation</a> and other transportation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Because of their wealth and the importance of energy, transport and chemical industries to local, national and international economies, these lobbies have the capacity and money to attempt to have outsized influence governmental policy. In particular, the lobbies have been known to obstruct policy related to <a href="/wiki/Environmental_protection" title="Environmental protection">environmental protection</a>, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_health" title="Environmental health">environmental health</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_Action" title="Climate Action">climate action</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lobbies are active in most fossil-fuel intensive economies with democratic governance, with reporting on the lobbies most prominent in Canada, Australia, the United States and Europe, however the lobbies are present in many parts of the world. <a href="/wiki/Big_Oil" title="Big Oil">Big Oil</a> companies such as <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">ExxonMobil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shell_plc" title="Shell plc">Shell</a>, <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a>, <a href="/wiki/TotalEnergies" title="TotalEnergies">TotalEnergies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron Corporation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ConocoPhillips" title="ConocoPhillips">ConocoPhillips</a> are among the largest <a href="/wiki/Corporation" title="Corporation">corporations</a> associated with the fossil fuels lobby.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_Petroleum_Institute" title="American Petroleum Institute">American Petroleum Institute</a> is a powerful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industry_lobbyist" title="Industry lobbyist">industry lobbyist</a> for Big Oil with significant clout in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuels_lobby_theguardian.com_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuels_lobby_theguardian.com-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuels_lobby_reutersevents.com_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuels_lobby_reutersevents.com-83">[83]</a></sup>
</p>
Some observers have also been critical of the presence of major fossil fuel companies at global forums for decision making, like the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuels_lobby_:1_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuels_lobby_:1-84">[84]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Climate Agreement</a> negotiations,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuels_lobby_:1_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuels_lobby_:1-84">[84]</a></sup> the Plastic  and other international forums. The lobby is known for exploiting international crises, such as the COVID-19 pandemic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuels_lobby_:2_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuels_lobby_:2-85">[85]</a></sup> or the <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuels_lobby_:3_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuels_lobby_:3-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> to try to roll back existing regulations or justify new fossil fuel development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuels_lobby_:2_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuels_lobby_:2-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fossil_fuels_lobby_:3_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fossil_fuels_lobby_:3-86">[86]</a></sup></div></div>

<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFReference-OED-fossil"><span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a class="external text" href="https://oed.com/search?searchType=dictionary&amp;q=fossil" rel="nofollow">"fossil"</a></span>. <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i> (Online ed.). <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" title="Oxford University Press">Oxford University Press</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=fossil&amp;rft.btitle=Oxford+English+Dictionary&amp;rft.edition=Online&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Foed.com%2Fsearch%3FsearchType%3Ddictionary%26q%3Dfossil&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFossil+fuel"></span> <span style="font-size:0.95em; font-size:95%; color:#555">(Subscription or <a class="external text" href="https://www.oed.com/public/login/loggingin#withyourlibrary" rel="nofollow">participating institution membership</a> required.)</span> – "fossil [...] adj. <li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFReference-OED-fossil"><span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a class="external text" href="https://oed.com/search?searchType=dictionary&amp;q=fossil" rel="nofollow">"fossil"</a></span>. <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i> (Online ed.). <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" title="Oxford University Press">Oxford University Press</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=fossil&amp;rft.btitle=Oxford+English+Dictionary&amp;rft.edition=Online&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Foed.com%2Fsearch%3FsearchType%3Ddictionary%26q%3Dfossil&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFossil+fuel"></span> <span style="font-size:0.95em; font-size:95%; color:#555">(Subscription or <a class="external text" href="https://www.oed.com/public/login/loggingin#withyourlibrary" rel="nofollow">participating institution membership</a> required.)</span> – "fossil [...] n. [...] Something preserved in the ground, esp. in petrified form in rock, and recognizable as the remains of a living organism of a former geological period, or as preserving an impression or trace of such an organism."</span>
